srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> 23.2%</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source: Flughafen Wien AG<sup id="cite_ref-2020results_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020results-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Vienna International Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Flughafen Wien-Schwechat</i>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>: <i lang="sk">Letisko Viede\xc5\x88-Schwechat</i>; <a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>VIE</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LOWW</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Schwechat" title="Schwechat">Schwechat</a>, 18&#160;km (11&#160;mi) southeast of central Vienna and 57 kilometres (35&#160;mi) west of <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>. It is the country\'s largest airport and serves as the hub for <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a> as well as a base for low-cost carriers <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>. It is capable of handling <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body aircraft</a> up to the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>. The airport features a dense network of European destinations as well as long-haul flights to <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. In 2020, the airport handled 7.8 million passengers, a 75.3% decrease compared to 2019 due to the <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_aviation" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on aviation">collapse of air traffic during the COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2020results_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020results-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" class="toctext">Accidents and incidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Originally built as a military airport in 1938, and used during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Heinkel" title="Heinkel">Heinkel</a> firm\'s southern military aircraft design and production complex, or <i>Heinkel-S\xc3\xbcd</i> facility, it was taken over by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> in 1945 and became RAF Schwechat under the occupation of the country. In 1954, the <i>Betriebsgesellschaft</i> was founded, and the airport replaced <a href="/wiki/Aspern" title="Aspern">Aspern</a> as Vienna\'s (and Austria\'s) principal aerodrome. There was just one <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runway</a>, which in 1959 was expanded to measure 3,000&#160;m (9,843&#160;ft). The erection of the new airport building starting in 1959.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 1972, another runway was built. In 1982 the airport was connected to the national motorway network (<a href="/wiki/Ostautobahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Ostautobahn">Ostautobahn</a>). In 1986 the enlarged arrivals hall was opened, and in 1988 Pier East with 8 jetbridges.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On 27 December 1985, the <a href="/wiki/El_Al" title="El Al">El Al</a> ticket counter was attacked by <a href="/wiki/Abu_Nidal" title="Abu Nidal">Abu Nidal</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian terrorism">Palestinian terrorist</a> organization that simultaneously conducted a <a href="/wiki/1985_Rome_and_Vienna_airport_attacks" title="1985 Rome and Vienna airport attacks">terrorist attack at Fiumicino Airport in Rome</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Flughafen_Wien_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Flughafen Wien AG">Flughafen Wien AG</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flughafen_Wien_AG" class="extiw" title="de:Flughafen Wien AG">de</a>&#93;</span>, one of the few publicly traded airport operators in Europe, was privatised in 1992. The state of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Austria" title="Lower Austria">Lower Austria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Vienna" class="mw-redirect" title="City of Vienna">City of Vienna</a> each hold 20% of the shares, the private employee participation foundation holds 10%, with the remaining 50% held privately.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The shares are part of the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Traded_Index" title="Austrian Traded Index">Austrian Traded Index</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 1992, the new Terminal 1 was opened and a year later the shopping area around the plaza in the transit area of the B, C and D gates. In 1996 Pier West with 12 jetbridges got in operation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_since_the_2000s">Development since the 2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development since the 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2006, the 109&#160;m (358&#160;ft) tall control tower started operating. It allows a free overview of the entire airport area and offers a night laser show, which should welcome the passengers even from the aircraft. From 2004 to 2007, an Office Park had been erected offering 69,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (740,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of rentable space. A VIP- and general aviation-terminal, including a separated apron, opened in 2006.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>To accommodate future growth, in 1998 Vienna Airport published a master plan that outlined expansion projects until 2015. These projects included a new office park, railway station, cargo center, general aviation center, air traffic control tower, terminal, and runway. Additionally, the plan called for streamlined security control.<sup id="cite_ref-2005_Annual_Report_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005_Annual_Report-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The centerpiece of the enlargement was the new terminal, dubbed Skylink during its construction. In 2002, the airport\'s management estimated that building the new terminal will cost <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a>401.79 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Court_of_Audit_cost_estimates_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Court_of_Audit_cost_estimates-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> However, costs skyrocketed and in 2009 stood at an estimated <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a>929.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Court_of_Audit_cost_estimates_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Court_of_Audit_cost_estimates-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The Austrian <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Audit" title="Court of Audit">Court of Audit</a> then recommended that the airport implement several cost-savings measures, which in the Court\'s estimate brought down final costs to <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a>849.15 million, still more than double the original plans.<sup id="cite_ref-Court_of_Audit_cost_estimates_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Court_of_Audit_cost_estimates-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On June 5, 2012, the new <i>Austrian Star Alliance Terminal</i> (Terminal 3, named <i>Skylink</i> during its construction) was opened, which enables the airport to handle up to 30 million passengers per year.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Construction started in 2004 and was suspended due to projected cost increases in 2009, but resumed in 2010. The maximum planned costs totaled less than \xe2\x82\xac770 million.<sup id="cite_ref-viennaairport.com_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-viennaairport.com-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Following concerns over the mismanagement of the Skylink project, chief executive Herbert Kaufman agreed to resign at the end of December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The new building with its North Pier has 17 jetbridges and makes the airport capable of handling more aircraft, although the new terminal is not able to handle <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> aircraft. However, the older Concourse D will see an upgrade to accommodate the A380.<sup id="cite_ref-2016refurbishment_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016refurbishment-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vienna_International_Airport_from_the_Air_Traffic_Control_Tower_08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vienna_International_Airport_from_the_Air_Traffic_Control_Tower_08.jpg/220px-Vienna_International_Airport_from_the_Air_Traffic_Control_Tower_08.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vienna_International_Airport_from_the_Air_Traffic_Control_Tower_08.jpg/330px-Vienna_International_Airport_from_the_Air_Traffic_Control_Tower_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vienna_International_Airport_from_the_Air_Traffic_Control_Tower_08.jpg/440px-Vienna_International_Airport_from_the_Air_Traffic_Control_Tower_08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="4016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vienna_International_Airport_from_the_Air_Traffic_Control_Tower_08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Concourse D seen from the tower showing the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> parking position</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vienna_airport_terminal_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Vienna_airport_terminal_3.jpg/220px-Vienna_airport_terminal_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Vienna_airport_terminal_3.jpg/330px-Vienna_airport_terminal_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Vienna_airport_terminal_3.jpg/440px-Vienna_airport_terminal_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6520" data-file-height="4347" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vienna_airport_terminal_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance hall of Terminal 3</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport has four terminal buildings named <i>Terminal 1, 2</i> and <i>3</i> which are directly built against each other as well as the additional <i>Terminal 1A</i> located opposite Terminal 1. Terminals 1, 2 and 3 connect to the five concourses. The central arrivals hall for all terminal areas is located in Terminal 3.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals_2">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>Terminal 1</b> underwent refurbishment in January 2013 and is now mainly used by some <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">oneworld</a> and <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> airlines and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 1A</b>, located in a standalone building opposite Terminal 1 hosts check-in facilities for a number of <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carriers</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 2</b> is currently closed, pending refurbishment.<sup id="cite_ref-2016refurbishment_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016refurbishment-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It was used by numerous foreign airlines whose check-in facilities have been primarily relocated to Terminal 1.</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 3</b>, also referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> Terminal, with its adjoining Concourses F and G is the airport\'s newest facility. It is used by the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines Group</a>, most <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> members, and a number of other carriers including <a href="/wiki/All_Nippon_Airways" title="All Nippon Airways">ANA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Al" title="El Al">El Al</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Jordanian" title="Royal Jordanian">Royal Jordanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways" title="Thai Airways">Thai Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a>.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Concourses">Concourses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Concourses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>Concourse B</b> is in the basement of Concourse C and features Gates B31\xe2\x80\x93B42 (boarding by buses) for Schengen destinations</li>\n<li><b>Concourse C</b> (<i>pier west</i>) for Schengen destinations; features Gates C31\xe2\x80\x93C42 (jetbridges), C71\xe2\x80\x93C75 (buses, Schengen only)</li>\n<li><b>Concourse D</b> (<i>pier east</i>; formerly <i>Concourse A</i>) for non-Schengen destinations with shared passport control at the entrance of pier east; features Gates D21\xe2\x80\x93D29 (boarding via jetbridges), D31\xe2\x80\x93D37 (boarding via buses), D61\xe2\x80\x93D70 (buses). Concourse D will be refurbished and equipped to handle the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> as part of the refurbishment programme announced in March 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-2016refurbishment_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016refurbishment-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Concourse F</b> (Level 1 of <i>pier north</i>) is used for Schengen destinations and consists of Gates F01-F37 (jetbridges and buses)</li>\n<li><b>Concourse G</b> (Level 3 and basement of <i>pier north</i>) for non-Schengen destinations; shared passport control at the entrance of Level 3; features Gates G01-G37 (jetbridges and busgates) and G61-67 (boarding via buses)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_projects">Expansion projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Expansion projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Vienna Airport originally projected that it would need a third runway by 2012, or 2016 at the latest, in the event of cooperation with nearby <a href="/wiki/Bratislava_Airport" title="Bratislava Airport">Bratislava Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2005_Annual_Report_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005_Annual_Report-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It currently projects that a third runway will be necessary by 2025,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> however, environmental organizations and some local communities oppose construction.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> These groups have attacked the decision of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Austria" title="Lower Austria">Lower Austria</a> (the state in which the airport is located) to move ahead with the first phase of construction; verdict from the administrative court that has taken up the lawsuit was expected later in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> As of September 2016, there were ongoing public protests while as no legal decision had been made.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> On 28 March 2018, the Austrian Federal Administrative Court ruled in favour of a third runway, a decision that may be appealed by opponents within six weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The third runway is planned to be parallel to and south of the existing runway 11/29. It will be designated 11R/29L, with the existing runway being renamed 11L/29R. The new runway is planned to be 3680 m long and 60 m wide, and equipped with a category III <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system" title="Instrument landing system">instrument landing system</a> in one direction (29L).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2019, the refurbishment of Terminal 2 started. Terminal 2 is planned to reopen in the end of 2020. Once Terminal 2 has been reopened, Concourse D will be closed for refurbishment at the beginning of 2021, it is expected to open again in 2023. In addition to that, a completely new building will be built. It will connect the existing pier east and pier north. The so-called T3 Southern Enlargement will be offering 70,000 m2 (750,000 sq ft) of  leisure  area and new additional bus gates. Opening is set for 2023.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="mw-redirect" title="EgyptAir">EgyptAir</a>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahnhof_VIE_-_Bahnsteige_Ost.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Bahnhof_VIE_-_Bahnsteige_Ost.JPG/220px-Bahnhof_VIE_-_Bahnsteige_Ost.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Bahnhof_VIE_-_Bahnsteige_Ost.JPG/330px-Bahnhof_VIE_-_Bahnsteige_Ost.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Bahnhof_VIE_-_Bahnsteige_Ost.JPG/440px-Bahnhof_VIE_-_Bahnsteige_Ost.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahnhof_VIE_-_Bahnsteige_Ost.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The airport\'s railway station</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Airport_railway_station" title="Vienna Airport railway station">Vienna Airport railway station</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Vienna_S-Bahn" title="Vienna S-Bahn">Vienna S-Bahn</a> line <a href="/wiki/S7_(Vienna)" title="S7 (Vienna)">S7</a> provides a local service to the city centre taking approx. 25 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The more expensive <a href="/wiki/City_Airport_Train" title="City Airport Train">City Airport Train</a> connects the airport directly to <a href="/wiki/Wien_Mitte_railway_station" title="Wien Mitte railway station">Wien Mitte railway station</a>, close to the city centre, in 16 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Additionally, the underground railway station has been expanded to accommodate long-distance trains. Since December 2014, the first trains passing <a href="/wiki/Wien_Hauptbahnhof" title="Wien Hauptbahnhof">Vienna\'s new main station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a> services from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, terminate at the airport. Since December 2015, <a href="/wiki/Railjet" title="Railjet">\xc3\x96BB Railjet</a> services operate to the airport as well. Long-distance train rides between the airport and the main station take approx. 15 minutes.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car">Car</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Car">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport lies directly adjacent to motorway A4 which leads from central <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> to <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>. It has its own exit named <i>Flughafen Wien-Schwechat</i>. <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> can be reached via motorway A6 which splits from the A4 in the east. Taxis and car rental facilities are available at the airport. There are also several taxi companies that operate at the airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Buses operate from the airport to various places in Vienna and to other cities including <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brno" title="Brno">Brno</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>In 1955, a <a href="/wiki/Convair_CV-340" class="mw-redirect" title="Convair CV-340">Convair CV-340</a> crashed on approach to the airport, killing 7 of the 29 passengers and crew on board. This is the last fatal aviation accident to occur at Wien-Schwechat Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 27 December 1985, terrorist attacks were carried out at Vienna and Rome Airports. Arab terrorists attacked the airports with assault rifles and hand grenades. In the Vienna attack three people were killed and 44 others were wounded. One terrorist was killed and two captured by police and security guards.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 12 July 2000, <a href="/wiki/Hapag-Lloyd_Flight_3378" title="Hapag-Lloyd Flight 3378">Hapag-Lloyd Flight 3378</a> crashed short of the runway at the airport on the final approach of its diverted flight due to <a href="/wiki/Fuel_exhaustion" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuel exhaustion">fuel exhaustion</a>. There were no fatalities, but the aircraft was damaged beyond repair.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Austria" title="Transport in Austria">Transport in Austria</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Austria" title="List of airports in Austria">List of airports in Austria</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
